## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration is determined by restoring forces (dependent on x), damping forces (dependent on v), and possibly time-dependent driving forces, with nonlinear terms distinguishing it from the simple harmonic oscillator.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (driven linear oscillator)
- Morse-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * x) * (1 - c2 * exp(c3 * x)) (anharmonic molecular potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — symmetric potential wells
- Even-power terms in position (x²) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells with different behavior for positive/negative displacement
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign determines which
- Products of x² and v (e.g., x²·v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators like van der Pol
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c·x) indicate a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum), replacing polynomial restoring forces
- Trigonometric functions of time sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or exchanged through velocity-dependent terms
- Rational functions of x like x/(1 + c·x²) can represent bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements

- `sin(c*t + c)` - depends on t, not v

- `exp(...)` terms - exponentials
- `log(c*v+1)`, `log(c*x+1)` - logarithms but not sin(v)

None can produce `sin(v)`.

Also checking: could the `log(|v|+1)` term be produced? The candidates with log have `log(c*v+1)` which equals `log(|v|+1)` only when v≥0 (with c=1). For all v, `log(|v|+1) ≠ log(cv+1)` for any constant c.

Even if we ignore the log issue, the `sin(v)` term is fundamentally absent from all candidates. No combination of the available terms can produce `sin(v)` for all values of v.
